  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_7b36ab84-59a5-4be7-a54a-ccecb41ebe3c'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<span id="freeTextContainer1902032636523549157">Jane Hayes is a seemingly normal young New Yorker, but she has a secret. Her obsession with Mr. Darcy, as played by Colin Firth in the BBC adaptation of <i>Pride and Prejudice</i>, is ruining her love life: no real man can compare. But when a wealthy relative bequeaths her a trip to an English resort catering to Austen-crazed women, Jane's fantasies of meeting the perfect Regency</span>
  <span id="freeText1902032636523549157" style="display:none">Jane Hayes is a seemingly normal young New Yorker, but she has a secret. Her obsession with Mr. Darcy, as played by Colin Firth in the BBC adaptation of <i>Pride and Prejudice</i>, is ruining her love life: no real man can compare. But when a wealthy relative bequeaths her a trip to an English resort catering to Austen-crazed women, Jane's fantasies of meeting the perfect Regency-era gentleman suddenly become realer than she ever could have imagined.<br /><br />Decked out in empire-waist gowns, Jane struggles to master Regency etiquette and flirts with gardeners and gentlemen;or maybe even, she suspects, with the actors who are playing them. It's all a game, Jane knows. And yet the longer she stays, the more her insecurities seem to fall away, and the more she wonders: Is she about to kick the Austen obsession for good, or could all her dreams actually culminate in a Mr. Darcy of her own?</span>
  <a data-text-id="1902032636523549157" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">No need to. It helps if you have at least a basic knowledge of the storylines of her books, because the author references them from time to time and t<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">No need to. It helps if you have at least a basic knowledge of the storylines of her books, because the author references them from time to time and there are elements of the stories found in the book, but if you've watched movie versions of them, that'd be more than enough info to follow what she's saying.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/16523051" />
    <a title="Lucy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/307208-lucy"><img alt="Lucy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1233177432p2/307208.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/16523051?book_show_action=true">Feb 27, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lucy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lucy" href="/user/show/307208-lucy">Lucy</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer16523051" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15666291570913632013">I am a Pride and Prejudice snob. I only like the BBC version, with Colin Firth as Mr. Darcy and Jennifer Ehle as Elizabeth Bennett. While there are parts of the newer, shorter, harried, and nuance free Hollywood version I enjoy, like the supposed-to-be-prettiest-sister Jane, who is actually much prettier than the actress in the BBC version, every time I've watched it (which, I grant, is only twice), I feel angry afterwards. First, Kiera Knightly is NOT Elizabeth Bennett. Elizabeth Bennett does n</span>
  <span id="freeText15666291570913632013" style="display:none">I am a Pride and Prejudice snob. I only like the BBC version, with Colin Firth as Mr. Darcy and Jennifer Ehle as Elizabeth Bennett. While there are parts of the newer, shorter, harried, and nuance free Hollywood version I enjoy, like the supposed-to-be-prettiest-sister Jane, who is actually much prettier than the actress in the BBC version, every time I've watched it (which, I grant, is only twice), I feel angry afterwards. First, Kiera Knightly is NOT Elizabeth Bennett. Elizabeth Bennett does not smile a ridiculous smile showing her bottom teeth all the time. And she is not flat chested. I mean, come on....we're talking about the girl who woos Mr. Darcy. With those low-cut gowns in style, I'm guessing there was a little bit of oomph necessary to catch his eye. That and a pair of "fine eyes". Mostly, though, the entire movie is rushed. The actors spit out their lines in Gilmore Girls fashion, important scenes are entirely cut out, and then two minutes are devoted to watching Kiera Knightly spin on a swing. Frustrating.<br /><br />Anyways, my point is (and I do have one), that there is only one good movie adaptation...and it's six hours long and only strays (and not really even strays, just leaves out a few minor details) slightly from the book. So, when the main character in Austenland, Jane, loved this movie as much as me, I knew I could appreciate her.<br /><br />32 year-old Jane, single and relationship challenged, is obsessed with Mr. Darcy...the dreamy Colin Firth who walks across his magnificent grounds in a wet shirt after diving into a pond (you know the scene). The Colin Firth...I mean Mr. Darcy, who beams at Elizabeth while she's turning pages for his sister, Georgiana, at the piano (you know this scene too). After her rich great aunt comes to visit her, and subsequently finds her two-disc DVDs hidden behind a houseplant, Jane is surprised when she receives a call following her aunt's death from the probate attorney. Instead of money, her aunt leaves her an all expense paid for trip to an exclusive British resort, where Jane will spend three weeks living the Regency period lifestyle in an attempt to fulfill, and also hopefully expunge, her Darcy obsession.<br /><br />I found the beginning of this book to be annoying. Jane is too nervous and melodramatic and not all that likable. For starters, I have no idea why anyone would be ashamed of owning Pride and Prejudice. Houseplants? Please. I'm thinking of fashioning my set up with a chain and wearing it around my neck. See? I'm a true fan.<br /><br />However, the three weeks she spends at Pembrook Park, a Netherfield/Pemberly-esque manor with servants who can't speak to her, empire wasted gowns, gentleman that are actors (or are they?), turns about the room, walks on the grounds and a ball are simply fantastic. The situations are entertaining, the plot pleasantly twisty and the ending satisfying.<br /><br />Shannon Hale writes a light-hearted fantasy romance that is sure to please even the snobbiest Jane Austen fans. As a warning, do not expect a Jane Austen book. While Hale does a fair job mimicking some of the dialogue, the novel is thoroughly modern and much less subtle. It is a romance...therefore extremely unlikely to be true. Regardless, when I turned the last page, I had a smile on my face and said, out loud, "That was fun!"</span>
  <a data-text-id="15666291570913632013" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_22318694" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/22318694" />
    <a title="Melinda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/969650-melinda"><img alt="Melinda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1369362393p2/969650.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/22318694?book_show_action=true">May 15, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melinda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melinda" href="/user/show/969650-melinda">Melinda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer22318694" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16151137601190375798">I crept quietly up the dark stairway, entered my room and tried my very best to shut the door silently behind me. It thudded despite my best efforts and I cringed, but Phil didn’t stir in his 3 o’clock-in-the-morning slumber. I sighed, relieved. <br/>I felt so entirely sneaky. I felt as if I had cheated and there was a sting of guilt as I looked at the distorted red figures on the alarm clock through the empty glass on the night stand. “Please don’t wake up and look at what I see” I silently begged t</span>
  <span id="freeText16151137601190375798" style="display:none">I crept quietly up the dark stairway, entered my room and tried my very best to shut the door silently behind me. It thudded despite my best efforts and I cringed, but Phil didn’t stir in his 3 o’clock-in-the-morning slumber. I sighed, relieved. <br />I felt so entirely sneaky. I felt as if I had cheated and there was a sting of guilt as I looked at the distorted red figures on the alarm clock through the empty glass on the night stand. “Please don’t wake up and look at what I see” I silently begged to the shadowy outline that was Phil. He didn’t. I climbed into bed and gave up all caution trying to snag a bit of the blanket so tightly wound around him. He turned over, releasing his tight hold on the blanket, and rested his leg on mine- still asleep. I relaxed and tried to sleep… but after reading for 5 hours on end- my mind was a frenzy of literature and as I closed my eyes, I could see words giving description to my every action. <br />From the satisfying moment I closed the book that I’d begun only hours prior and ascended to the sleepy second floor of our home- my motions were narrated perfectly in my head. I laughed it off, and enjoyed the silliness of my thoughts. It reminded me of how Phil had once told me about a fishing trip with the guys’. They’d spent so many hours cleaning their vast catch that when he went to bed he continued cleaning fish behind his closed lids. That had to be what was happening to me, luckily it was prose and not smelly fish guts stealing my rest! <br />Finally, I did sleep, though it was a heavy, dreamless-sleep. It is rare thing, for me, not to dream. It was as though I had traded, for the night, my own colorful, unpredictable imagination for the author’s. I needed no dreams or contemplations tonight.<br />So, this is my curse. I cannot pick up a good book and put it down, I must read it’s entirety before I can rest. I had gotten the call from the library yesterday afternoon that the book I had requested from a neighboring library had come in. Yes, yes… another Shannon Hale masterpiece, if you must pry! I wasn’t so sure I would like this one. I like Jane Austen, but wouldn’t call myself a fan (yet). I haven’t read any of her books, and while I enjoyed some of the movies based on them, I hesitate to admit I’d felt they were dry and hard to follow at times. <br />So, I used the excuse that I needed to return a few of the books (which, I had only borrowed last Friday), so I could sneak over to the Library on my way to work. I don’t know why I felt the urge to keep this a secret. Phil doesn’t mind in any way, that I love reading. Perhaps it heightened the appeal and experience of reading it? I knew if I worked quickly I could have time to begin the book before heading home, and how wonderful a thing- to read without any interruptions. <br />Maybe that’s just what it was. If I am openly preoccupied with something- it’s a trigger. That is when everyone needs some-thing! So, I read the book from start to finish, unburdened by distraction. <br />And why am I publishing these thoughts to a review? Does anyone actually care? Probably not so much- but I had the urge to type out my own thoughts to cleanse my eyelids so that I might relinquish my own dreams tonight. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16151137601190375798" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_8590718" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/8590718" />
    <a title="Lorraine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/573080-lorraine"><img alt="Lorraine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1193177650p2/573080.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/8590718?book_show_action=true">Nov 02, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lorraine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lorraine" href="/user/show/573080-lorraine">Lorraine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Austen fans and Romantics</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/573080-lorraine?shelf=american">american</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/573080-lorraine?shelf=chick-lit">chick-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/573080-lorraine?shelf=british">british</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer8590718" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15326070952230744825"><br/>I was so engrossed in this book I read it in an afternoon. If I were still a teenager, this would be the book I'd read over and over.<br/><br/>I hate this book. <br/><br/>SPOILER ALERT<br/><br/>Why? I mean, if it was so engrossing that I couldn't put it down, why do I hate it? Because Jane Hayes, the main character, is me except that she gets to live out my fantasy and gets the happy ending only found in Austen novels.<br/><br/>Jane is in her early 30s, in a job she likes but does not love, convinced she must embrace her spinsterhood.</span>
  <span id="freeText15326070952230744825" style="display:none"><br />I was so engrossed in this book I read it in an afternoon. If I were still a teenager, this would be the book I'd read over and over.<br /><br />I hate this book. <br /><br />SPOILER ALERT<br /><br />Why? I mean, if it was so engrossing that I couldn't put it down, why do I hate it? Because Jane Hayes, the main character, is me except that she gets to live out my fantasy and gets the happy ending only found in Austen novels.<br /><br />Jane is in her early 30s, in a job she likes but does not love, convinced she must embrace her spinsterhood. So far, so good. I relate completely. Her secret vice is Pride and Prejudice (more the BBC movie than the novel) and she is in love with Mr. Darcy. For me, it's more Rhett Butler, but the implication is there. A great-aunt spots this fantasy and bequeaths to Jane a three-week stay at Austenland, a resort in England where people live like characters in an Austen novel. I have always thought I was born in the wrong century; this vacation would be a dream for me. Jane gets to live out her fantasy and deal with her obsession of Mr. Darcy. I get to read about it.<br /><br />Okay, differences: Jane is beautiful; she turns heads. At the beginning each chapter, a synopsis is given of each of Jane's ex-boyfriends. There are 13. Plus her "first love" (at age four) and three other "Guys". If I were the main character, there couldn't be so many chapters; only First Love, Boyfriend #6, Guy Between #6 and 7, #7, #10, and maybe Guy After #12 would work in my story (read the book: you'll get how sad that is). Jane makes out with the gardner, attracts the men at Pembroke...it's all very ideal. <br /><br />Without the same finesse and fine writing of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1265.Jane_Austen" title="Jane Austen" rel="nofollow noopener">Austen</a>, (this book really qualifies as chicklit, not fine literature) <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/49177.Shannon_Hale" title="Shannon Hale" rel="nofollow noopener">Shannon Hale</a> does echo an Austen-like story. Underlying commentary on the absurdity of relationships and women's fantasy loves are clear. But the end is so inevitable and apparent you hope for a surprise twist. She gets her guy in the end, just like in Pride and Prejudice.<br /><br />So why do I hate it? Jane Hayes goes to Austenland hoping to rid herself of the dream that one day she'll meet her Mr. Darcy and be swept off her feet. I really hoped this book would put to rest the romantic ideal I and many other women harbour. That finally there would be a book where the heroine found happiness without a man. Instead, this book perpetuates the dream. To a 'tee'.<br /><br />And I have to return to the real world.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15326070952230744825" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

But the author of this book seems to have written mostly children's books before, and this struck me as a children's book ... but for women. And not even a well-written children's book. The dialogue in spots was read-out-loud bad and the main character was fla</span>
  <span id="freeText7370704791522625442" style="display:none">I read this book all the way through only because I love Jane Austen, and because the concept of the book was quirky and irresisistible. It kind of felt like eating an entire bag of cotton candy. <br />I guess I just don't like chick lit, maybe. But the author of this book seems to have written mostly children's books before, and this struck me as a children's book ... but for women. And not even a well-written children's book. The dialogue in spots was read-out-loud bad and the main character was flat and just not believable. (At least, she wasn't like any grown woman I've ever met.) Her "transformation" was forced and shallow.<br />I have to admit I did like the ending, though. It was cute and I at least felt a little bit of payoff for finishing the book.</span>

<div id="review_170181945" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/170181945" />
    <a title="Brandy Painter" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2840210-brandy-painter"><img alt="Brandy Painter" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1398019139p2/2840210.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/170181945?book_show_action=true">May 22, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brandy Painter" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brandy Painter" href="/user/show/2840210-brandy-painter">Brandy Painter</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2840210-brandy-painter?shelf=contemporary-fiction">contemporary-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2840210-brandy-painter?shelf=adult-fiction">adult-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer170181945" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8662193745472350365">I can't believe I just gave one star to a Shannon Hale book. Never thought that would happen.<br/><br/>Review originally posted <a href='http://brandy-painter.livejournal.com/36898.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>here</a>.<br/><br/>I really like Shannon Hale's books. And I love Jane Austen. It has taken me this long to get around to reading Shannon Hale's Austenland because I had a suspicion I might be disappointed. The book is a light quick read perfect for summer reading. If you are fan of romantic comedy, either in chick lit or chick flick form, then you might enjoy it. If you are a Jane Austen fan.</span>
  <span id="freeText8662193745472350365" style="display:none">I can't believe I just gave one star to a Shannon Hale book. Never thought that would happen.<br /><br />Review originally posted <a href="http://brandy-painter.livejournal.com/36898.html" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a>.<br /><br />I really like Shannon Hale's books. And I love Jane Austen. It has taken me this long to get around to reading Shannon Hale's Austenland because I had a suspicion I might be disappointed. The book is a light quick read perfect for summer reading. If you are fan of romantic comedy, either in chick lit or chick flick form, then you might enjoy it. If you are a Jane Austen fan....it is going to depend on what type of Jane Austen fan you are. If you are in the camp that loves her books (and more than the books the period movie adaptations of them) because they are Regency romances that are historical chick lit (or flicks) then you might also enjoy this. Neither of these things being true about me, I didn't. In fact I have some rather major issues with it. I almost feel bad about this because I do really really like Shannon Hale's other books. I almost wasn't going to write a review I felt so bad, but I have been stewing over this for a couple of days and just want to get some of it off my chest.<br /><br />I had issues with Jane. The same issues I have with all of the similar characters to her that seem to be cropping up more and more in this type of book or movie. Jane is a single successful woman with a career and life (sort of) in New York City. Yet she is a mess because she is a desperate husband hungry crazy girl. Why do women keep getting portrayed like this? We are meant to believe that these girls are savvy enough to graduate from college, secure a job, keep a job, live within their means in a large metropolis and yet they can't wear high heels without (at some point) falling over on their bottoms? (How many times is that shtick going to be used????) I have big problems with the whole idea that a woman can not be content and completely free of desperation if she doesn't have a boyfriend/husband. Each chapter of this book is introduced with a history of one of Jane's failed relationships. These highlight exactly how crazy desperate she is for this kind of relationship. Of course they have all failed. Men tend to run screaming scared from crazy women.<br /><br />Irony: Jane is exactly the sort of woman Jane Austen was making fun with her books. <br /><br />Because that is what her books are, not romantic frolics in period gowns, but social satires. At first I thought maybe the irony was intentional. And it may have been, but it fell fall short of its mark if it was. There is one point when Jane has an epiphany and realizes that she is not Elizabeth Bennet, but more like Mrs. Bennet. I expected things to turn around maybe, and that she would become more than she was, but the change that occurred wasn't one that had me believing in its longevity. While the Jane that leaves Austenland has more confidence and has convinced herself she was not looking for a Mr. Darcy duplicate, she never convinced me she was cured. In fact, the end makes it abundantly clear that she's not. More confident, less desperate, but given where she started she still has a long way to go. Except she got her storybook ending, so where is the motivation to grow? <br /><br />It was so frustrating.<br /><br />The frustration was probably greater for me because I know Shannon Hale can write strong female characters better than this. The girls in her Books of Bayern: amazing. Same goes for the girls in Princess Academy. Actually, Shannon Hale can just write better than this period. Honestly, if someone gave me this book to read without telling me who wrote it I never would have believed it to be Shannon Hale.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8662193745472350365" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer12791855454596434478">4+ stars for this Austen-inspired romantic comedy. <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1543947183ra/26686974.gif' width='400' height='165' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><i>Austenland</i> has an irresistible premise for me: a vacation getaway in England for ladies who can’t get enough of Mr Darcy or other Jane Austen heroes and want to pretend to live in her world for a few weeks. Jane’s great-aunt becomes aware of her Darcy obsession. A while later, when her great-aunt dies, Jane is stunned to find out that she has willed Jane an overseas trip to Austenland, where hired actors do their best to make wealthy ladies’ Reg</span>
  <span id="freeText12791855454596434478" style="display:none">4+ stars for this Austen-inspired romantic comedy. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1543947183ra/26686974.gif" width="400" height="165" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>Austenland</i> has an irresistible premise for me: a vacation getaway in England for ladies who can’t get enough of Mr Darcy or other Jane Austen heroes and want to pretend to live in her world for a few weeks. Jane’s great-aunt becomes aware of her Darcy obsession. A while later, when her great-aunt dies, Jane is stunned to find out that she has willed Jane an overseas trip to Austenland, where hired actors do their best to make wealthy ladies’ Regency dreams come true, if only for a short time. Jane isn’t wealthy, at all, but she really wants the Austen Experience.<br><br>Some people are better at the whole Regency-immersion thing than others. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1543946995ra/26686966.gif" width="345" height="202" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>It’s kind of hilarious because everyone in Austenland mostly ignores the rules that don’t appeal. Ladies get to wear makeup along with their corsets and empire-waisted dresses. Cell phones are a big NO, though. <br><br>Jane wavers between two guys: Mr Nobley, the one who’s clearly meant to be a Darcy type of character, and Martin, a tall, good-looking guy who mostly just takes care of the grounds. What is real and what is fake gets murky for Jane, as she kind of bounces back and forth between Mr Nobley and Martin, trying to figure out what she really wants. Something REAL, she thinks, but is that even possible in Austenland?<br><br>It’s a light, fun contemporary romance, with enough Austen to it to tickle my fancy. Maybe not for Austen purists, but I got a huge kick out of it. I’ve probably read it three times over the years.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1543946995ra/26686965.gif" width="280" height="280" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I think maybe it’s about time to read it again.<br><br>P.S. The movie was okay but a lot more slapstick. I liked the book a lot better, personally.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer1603439764983096424">I went into <b>Austenland</b> hoping for a fun and lighthearted book. It delivered!<br/><b>3.5 stars!</b><br/><br/>Like the main character Jane Hayes, I am also a fan of <b>Pride and Predjudice</b>. I read this book by <i>Jane Austen</i> at an early age and have loved historical romance since then. When I saw friends on this site reading <b>Austenland</b> earlier this year, I had to check it out!<br/><br/>Jane Hayes is 32, single and has problems staying in relationships. She’s obsessed with Mr. Darcy and has unrealistic expectations for men. Her rich, g</span>
  <span id="freeText1603439764983096424" style="display:none">I went into <b>Austenland</b> hoping for a fun and lighthearted book. It delivered!<br /><b>3.5 stars!</b><br /><br />Like the main character Jane Hayes, I am also a fan of <b>Pride and Predjudice</b>. I read this book by <i>Jane Austen</i> at an early age and have loved historical romance since then. When I saw friends on this site reading <b>Austenland</b> earlier this year, I had to check it out!<br /><br />Jane Hayes is 32, single and has problems staying in relationships. She’s obsessed with Mr. Darcy and has unrealistic expectations for men. Her rich, great aunt finds out about her obsession and pays for an all-inclusive trip to an estate in Great Britain called Pembrook Park.<br /><br />Pembrook Park reenacts the lifestyle back in the 1800s with full dress, manners, balls and servants. Jane cannot break character and must interact with gentleman and other ladies during this time period.<br />Is everyone acting or is anyone real in this Darcy obsessed place?! And that’s where Jane starts having issues. It looks like she loves New York City more then she thought. She’s getting bored with Whist, walking around the gardens and embroidery!<br /><br />The dialogue was good, the romance was fun, and this was a quick book to read. I will definitely read the second book in this series because I enjoyed how <i>Shannon Hale</i> weaved this funny and quirky romance set during the Regency times!</span>

<div id="review_74435003" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/74435003" />
    <a title="Tatiana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2250020-tatiana"><img alt="Tatiana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1249783659p2/2250020.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/74435003?book_show_action=true">Oct 13, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tatiana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tatiana" href="/user/show/2250020-tatiana">Tatiana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audible Audio " href="/book/show/1151489.Austenland">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">those who will read anything that  has Darcy in it</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=chick-lit">chick-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=2009">2009</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer74435003" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5330476121616030193">Seriously, I don't even know why I bother to read any P&P sequels, prequels, re-tellings, or books "inspired" by P&P. They all end up being a complete and utter nonsense (with the exception of "Bridget Jones' Diaries"). "Austenland" is no exception, unfortunately.<br/><br/>The premise of the book is OK. 33-year old Jane Hayes is single and obsessed with "Pride and Prejudice" Mr. Darcy (just like you are, admit it, otherwise you wouldn't be reading this review). She inherits a 3-week vacation to "Austenlan</span>
  <span id="freeText5330476121616030193" style="display:none">Seriously, I don't even know why I bother to read any P&amp;P sequels, prequels, re-tellings, or books "inspired" by P&amp;P. They all end up being a complete and utter nonsense (with the exception of "Bridget Jones' Diaries"). "Austenland" is no exception, unfortunately.<br /><br />The premise of the book is OK. 33-year old Jane Hayes is single and obsessed with "Pride and Prejudice" Mr. Darcy (just like you are, admit it, otherwise you wouldn't be reading this review). She inherits a 3-week vacation to "Austenland" - an English estate where guests get a taste of Austen-time living (and maybe romance) with the help of local actors. Jane agrees to the journey hoping to make it her farewell to Darcy fantasy and to move on with her life afterward. What follows is a chick-lit story with a vague directionless plot, a luke-warm romance, and a contrived plot "twist." <br /><br />The story never really takes off IMO, the book is void of real humor or passion, the heroine's inner thoughts and tribulations are hard to understand or follow. In the end, you fail to understand even if this Austenland trip is helpful or not: does it help you to cure your Darcy addiction by exposing the dullness of 19th-century living? or does it enhance it by experiencing a Darcy-like romance (which IMO makes the entire place seem like a some kind of expensive role-playing brothel)? I guess I'll never know...<br /><br />Don't get me wrong, the book isn't a complete disaster. There are some entertaining moments, but to be honest, I probably wouldn't have finished it were I not listening to it. <br /><br />Speaking of the audio, I think it is reasonable to expect from a person who narrates a book set in England to be able to do some English accent. The narrator of this book couldn't do English accent to save her life! It was rather sad actually...<br /><br />Reading challenge: #1 - H</span>
  <a data-text-id="5330476121616030193" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">
          

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review74435003">
  <td colspan="2">

<div id="review_31425593" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/31425593" />
    <a title="Rachelle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/770510-rachelle"><img alt="Rachelle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1417641728p2/770510.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/31425593?book_show_action=true">Aug 28, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rachelle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rachelle" href="/user/show/770510-rachelle">Rachelle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer31425593" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4280623714225550907">I picked up this book at about 10:30 last night thinking that I would just read the prologue to get the basic idea and then start it tomorrow. Alas... it was not meant to be. After about a half hour I whispered an apology to Aaron and slipped out of bed to go read in the living room. After reading late into the night and a quick nap (okay 5 1/2 hours) I got up this morning and didn't stop until I finished it. This book is so entertaining. I read a lot and I have often had a book bring me to tear</span>
  <span id="freeText4280623714225550907" style="display:none">I picked up this book at about 10:30 last night thinking that I would just read the prologue to get the basic idea and then start it tomorrow. Alas... it was not meant to be. After about a half hour I whispered an apology to Aaron and slipped out of bed to go read in the living room. After reading late into the night and a quick nap (okay 5 1/2 hours) I got up this morning and didn't stop until I finished it. This book is so entertaining. I read a lot and I have often had a book bring me to tears... but I honestly can't remember the last time I read a book that had me laughing out loud through the entire thing. The main character is obsessed with Jane Austen's writings and particularly with the BBC version of Pride and Prejudice starring Colin Firth (If you haven't seen it you can borrow mine and if you don't want to see it then believe me this book is not for you.) The book is stuffed full of Jane Austen's best lines and references to her timeless characters. And yet... they clash with Jane Hayes modern world in such a funny way (example: "Jane announced to the empty room, 'if you're listening, Big Brother, I refuse to be Fanny Price.'') When reading other reviews of this book.... there were not many raving reviews like mine so I have to realize that it is perhaps not the most well written book of all time... but for me, who related to the main character in (almost) every way... it was PERFECT. I have watched the same parts of Pride and Prejudice over and over just like the main character - and even though I am (somewhat) embarrassed by it - (just like the main character)... I don't expect to ever get over my obsession. I'm glad that Jane Hayes doesn't either.... she just has to find her own Mr. Darcy. </span>
  <a data-text-id="4280623714225550907" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_5190092" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/5190092" />
    <a title="Eviltwinjen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/284205-eviltwinjen"><img alt="Eviltwinjen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1187745574p2/284205.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/5190092?book_show_action=true">Aug 27, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Eviltwinjen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Eviltwinjen" href="/user/show/284205-eviltwinjen">Eviltwinjen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Chick lit fans, Austen fans who don't mind chick lit</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/284205-eviltwinjen?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/284205-eviltwinjen?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer5190092" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14357111725809883003">Jane Hayes is a single thirty-something with a string of no-good boyfriends and an unhealthy obsession with Mr. Darcy from <i>Pride and Prejudice</i>. Didn't someone already write that book, you say? Banish thoughts of Bridget Jones from your mind, because Shannon Hale knows her Austen. A true knowledge and love of the novels that spawned the fantasy lifts <i>Austenland</i> above its chick-lit peers.<br/><br/>The fabulous conceit of the novel is that there's a Regency-era mansion in England that hosts an exclusive vaca</span>
  <span id="freeText14357111725809883003" style="display:none">Jane Hayes is a single thirty-something with a string of no-good boyfriends and an unhealthy obsession with Mr. Darcy from <i>Pride and Prejudice</i>. Didn't someone already write that book, you say? Banish thoughts of Bridget Jones from your mind, because Shannon Hale knows her Austen. A true knowledge and love of the novels that spawned the fantasy lifts <i>Austenland</i> above its chick-lit peers.<br /><br />The fabulous conceit of the novel is that there's a Regency-era mansion in England that hosts an exclusive vacation experience for wealthy customers. Visitors dress in period clothes and live a period life for three weeks, interacting with actors and (they hope) having a little Austen-style romance. A wealthy, eccentric relative sends Jane Hayes to Pembrook Park, hoping it will cure her of her Darcy-lust and enable her to get on with her life. Despite her initial discomfort with the play-acting, Jane Hayes is soon enmeshed in the realities of playing Austen--the stultifying boredom of a well-bred lady's days, the richness of the language, the thrill of flirting when actual physical contact is taboo. Of course, there's a Mr. Darcy-like gentleman there (and a hot gardener), but will Jane recognize her real Mr. Darcy when she sees him?<br /><br />This is chick lit, yes, so there's a bit of treacle and a bit of "I'm a strong, independent woman...ooh, I slipped in my three-inch heels!", but Hale has an excellent command of Austen's dialog and a sharp eye for her heroine's insecurities and her dawning wisdom. <i>Austenland</i> is a lovely little book, totally satisfying, with just enough substance. I especially appreciate the fact that Jane finds not only her inner Elizabeth Bennett but her inner Mrs. Bennett, Lydia, Emma Woodhouse, and even her inner Darcy.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14357111725809883003" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer21846534" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8340834198214146712">This book was horrendous, certainly not worth anyone's time to read it. I loved her children's books, so I was excited to see that she wrote an adult book about Jane Austen (a serious departure from her usual subjects, which turned out to be a serious mistake). This book was basically Bridget Jones, minus any snarkiness, and with a huge dose of sincerity. Horrendous. (I loved Bridget Jones, but it was bearable/lovable BECAUSE of its snarkiness and level of self awareness). Worst of all, it's set</span>
  <span id="freeText8340834198214146712" style="display:none">This book was horrendous, certainly not worth anyone's time to read it. I loved her children's books, so I was excited to see that she wrote an adult book about Jane Austen (a serious departure from her usual subjects, which turned out to be a serious mistake). This book was basically Bridget Jones, minus any snarkiness, and with a huge dose of sincerity. Horrendous. (I loved Bridget Jones, but it was bearable/lovable BECAUSE of its snarkiness and level of self awareness). Worst of all, it's set in a current day Jane Austen camp, where losers play at being in a Jane Austen novel, complete with actors played to court them. And of course, the protagonist of this novel falls in love with the Mr. Darcy type actor. Just as uncomfortable as it sounds. I was really disappointed in this book. I was hoping for some chick lit with a brain, and I got maybe the worst chick lit I've ever read (and I've read some doozies). </span>

<div id="review_264748457" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

<span id="freeTextContainer7532259349534487716">To start with: The book is 100% better than the movie!<br/><br/>Ever wished you could dive into Pride & Prejudice and live there amongst the Bennets and Darcys and Bingleys?   <span id="freeText7532259349534487716" style="display:none">To start with: The book is 100% better than the movie!<br><br>Ever wished you could dive into Pride &amp; Prejudice and live there amongst the Bennets and Darcys and Bingleys? Like, for real? YEAH, ME TOO. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1531750797ra/25981983.gif" width="480" height="279" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Enter: Austenland. <br><br>This book was hilarious from the get-go, and completely sucked me in. It truly was a "nose-stuck-in-your-book" sort of book; I couldn't stop reading! Jane is such a funny and relatable character and I was rooting for her from the start. She is obsessed with Jane Austen's works and the worlds within them, and because of that can never seem to find real-life love. After all, who can compare to Mr. Darcy?<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1523325319ra/25352272.gif" width="480" height="203" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>(answer: no one can)<br><br>So when Jane's wealthy relative bequeaths to her a trip to Pembrook Park in England - a sort of theme park for Austen fans where you role play a Regency romance - Jane is skeptical (and embarrassed) but finally decides to go on the hope it might "cure" her of her Austen obsession.<br><br>So at first she's like:<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1479244470ra/21165253.gif" width="480" height="270" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And then she arrives to a world of Regency rules where no phones are allowed, conversation is carefully curated, and everyone seems to be playing a fictional role and she's like:<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1508399011ra/24208999.gif" width="480" height="270" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I absolutely loved reading about the crazy, semi-fictional world Jane was thrust into, and Pembrook Park was filled with hilarity, misadventure, and of course, romance. The book even had a few twists and revelations that I wasn't expecting at all!<br><br>Overall, this is a great, fun book full of witty, sharp characters and an entertaining plot. It's a must read for Austen fans, but also for anyone at all who enjoys an engaging read!</span>

<div id="review_1244410858" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1244410858" />
    <a title="Duchess Nicole" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2204947-duchess-nicole"><img alt="Duchess Nicole" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1499265843p2/2204947.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2204947-duchess-nicole?shelf=3-star-read">3-star-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2204947-duchess-nicole?shelf=read-in-2015">read-in-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2204947-duchess-nicole?shelf=genre-chick-lit">genre-chick-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2204947-duchess-nicole?shelf=heroine-tstl">heroine-tstl</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2204947-duchess-nicole?shelf=humorous">humorous</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1244410858" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5653091984867631687">I would never label myself as an Austen snob, or more specifically a Pride and Prejudice snob. I've read the original multiple times and I've read a handful of spinoffs, satires, and continuations, and I tend to love them all. I also pretty much love all the movie/TV adaptations, even though I do have my favorites. It all centers around the brooding, aloof, prideful gamma hero Darcy, of course. And I just love getting little glimpses into other P&P lover's ideas of this much-loved couple. I'm ge</span>
  <span id="freeText5653091984867631687" style="display:none">I would never label myself as an Austen snob, or more specifically a Pride and Prejudice snob. I've read the original multiple times and I've read a handful of spinoffs, satires, and continuations, and I tend to love them all. I also pretty much love all the movie/TV adaptations, even though I do have my favorites. It all centers around the brooding, aloof, prideful gamma hero Darcy, of course. And I just love getting little glimpses into other P&amp;P lover's ideas of this much-loved couple. I'm generally scornful of those who look down their nose at certain renditions of Austen's arguably most-loved book. I mean, only the original is perfection, right? Anything that centers on a love for Austen gets a thumbs up in my opinion.<br /><br />This ended up being very much a chick-lit book. Very low angst, very little romance, very little detail. It was honestly just a silly, somewhat vapid novel. But it was fun, it was based on a love of all things Austen and Darcy (though Captain Wentworth really gives Darcy a run for his money) and what's not to like about that? <br /><br />Jane's character was basically the same as the book...silly, vapid, uber girly and indecisive, and really not someone I can relate to...except for the fact that we share an obsessive love for fictional men. <br /><br />I plan on watching the movie, so I must have liked it okay.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5653091984867631687" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2826279586" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2826279586" />
    <a title="Anne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18780551-anne"><img alt="Anne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1520389159p2/18780551.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2826279586?book_show_action=true">May 26, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anne" href="/user/show/18780551-anne">Anne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781596912861" href="/book/show/2004362.Austenland">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18780551-anne?shelf=dear-sir-i-am-in-love-with-you">dear-sir-i-am-in-love-with-you</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18780551-anne?shelf=darling-books-i-want-to-hug">darling-books-i-want-to-hug</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18780551-anne?shelf=gentleman-like-heroes">gentleman-like-heroes</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18780551-anne?shelf=precious-little-gems">precious-little-gems</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18780551-anne?shelf=regency">regency</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18780551-anne?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18780551-anne?shelf=cotton-candy-fluff">cotton-candy-fluff</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18780551-anne?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18780551-anne?shelf=jane-austen-related">jane-austen-related</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18780551-anne?shelf=swoony-heroes">swoony-heroes</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2826279586" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4895772773656050971"><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1543947183ra/26686974.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Just like it's hard to resist the wonderful world of <i>Pride and Prejudice</i> (whether we're talking about the actual novel or the swoon-worthy '95 movie version...), likewise is it hard to resist the lure of <i>Austenland</i>. <br/><br/>The relatable and witty commentary of Jane <s>Hayes</s> Erstwhile as well as the fun, perfectly escape-worthy setting are really what make this book a little gem. It's nothing extraordinary, let's not fool ourselves, but there is something incredibly refreshing in its simplicity and direct </span>
  <span id="freeText4895772773656050971" style="display:none"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1543947183ra/26686974.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Just like it's hard to resist the wonderful world of <i>Pride and Prejudice</i> (whether we're talking about the actual novel or the swoon-worthy '95 movie version...), likewise is it hard to resist the lure of <i>Austenland</i>. <br><br>The relatable and witty commentary of Jane <s>Hayes</s> Erstwhile as well as the fun, perfectly escape-worthy setting are really what make this book a little gem. It's nothing extraordinary, let's not fool ourselves, but there is something incredibly refreshing in its simplicity and direct approach to an Austenite's problematic obsession with fantasy (including one Mr. Darcy in a wet shirt - played by Colin Firth, of course). <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1558894768ra/27575047.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Mr. Darcy has become such a staple of the modern girl's classy gentleman dream. <br>"So, anyone in your life?" they ask you, again and again.<br>"Ahhhhh. *cough* No, 'afraid not..." you invariably respond.<br>"*Deep sigh* Still waiting for Mr. Darcy, eh?". <br><br>You know what I mean. <b>It is a truth universally acknowledged that a single woman who reads Jane Austen must invariably raise her standards in love.</b> It's not that we all want Mr. Darcy, but rather that we come to appreciate the old-fashioned charm attached to him and other heroes of and around the Regency period. The mannerisms, the careful restraint, the gallantry... some of us just sigh in despair at today's standards of "dating" and would rather have our hand reverently kissed <br> over lustful making-out on a first date. It's not that we don't want passion - we most certainly <i>do</i> - but one slowly and carefully built, made all the more tantalizing by the waiting and the restraining, that comes to really <i>mean</i> something in the long-run. <br><br>This is part of what's meant when we say we are "waiting for Mr. Darcy". Just plain good old-fashioned romance. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1558894768ra/27575048.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Is it a fantasy? Sure. Romance in real-life rarely unfolds like romance in novels, but that doesn't mean you should lower your standards, let alone <i>settle</i>, heaven forbid. Just be realistic, and above all <b>be patient</b>. <br><br>The book's exploration of the fine line between having standards and living in an impossible fantasy were both highly amusing and very realistic, which for me raised it above the typical rom-com chick-lit it appears to be at first. <br><br>Of course, it <i>is</i> a rom-com and there is a happily-ever-after and a fantasy come true, but come on, how utterly disappointing would it be without it, and how boring would the story be without the heart-melting Mr. Nobley? <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1558894768ra/27575050.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I dare anyone to resist JJ Feild as a romantic hero. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1558894768ra/27575049.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>I mean, COME ON!<br><br>I suspect that the fact that I had already seen the movie adaptation of <i>Austenland</i> added to my enjoyment of the novel because I could already just picture JJ Feild as Mr. Nobley in my mind, but regardless (we are trying not to fantasize here, and be sensible!) it was a super fun, light-hearted book I enjoyed a lot and heartily recommend to my fellow Austenites who are equally enamoured with Jane Austen, Mr. Darcy, and being the heroine of our own story. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1558894768ra/27575051.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Also, Miss Charming and Miss Heartwright are absolutely hilarious in the movie, and they need their own real happily-ever-afters as well (there goes the romantic in me again...).<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1558894768ra/27575052.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>PS- What's up with the <i>Northanger Abbey</i> ill-feelings? <i>"Sure, Jane had first read </i>Pride and Prejudice<i> when she was sixteen, read it a dozen times since, and read the other Austen novels at least twice, except </i>Northanger Abbey<i> (of course)."</i> And why, pray tell, is <i>Northanger Abbey</i> thus slighted? <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1558894768ra/27575053.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>IT'S WONDERFUL AND ALSO STARS JJ FEILD AS AN IRRESISTIBLE HENRY-HERO AND DESERVES TO BE SHOWERED WITH LOVE (and for other reasons than just the hero). <br><br>*Off to go re-watch Northanger Abbey to make up for this singling out*</span>
  <a data-text-id="4895772773656050971" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer15202727083336264789">Jane Hayes is obsessed with Mr. Darcy. More particularly Colin Firth’s portrayal of Mr. Darcy in the film version of Pride and Prejudice. Can you blame her? Really? But, it might have something to do with why the thirty-three yeah old Jane is still unmarried and single. Her obsession for Mr. Darcy keeps any "real" man from measuring up.<br/><br/>Jane’s Aunt Carolyn is aware of her obsession. When Aunt Carolyn passes away she leaves Jane an all expense paid vacation to Pembrook Park, a resort that lets its</span>
  <span id="freeText15202727083336264789" style="display:none">Jane Hayes is obsessed with Mr. Darcy. More particularly Colin Firth’s portrayal of Mr. Darcy in the film version of Pride and Prejudice. Can you blame her? Really? But, it might have something to do with why the thirty-three yeah old Jane is still unmarried and single. Her obsession for Mr. Darcy keeps any "real" man from measuring up.<br /><br />Jane’s Aunt Carolyn is aware of her obsession. When Aunt Carolyn passes away she leaves Jane an all expense paid vacation to Pembrook Park, a resort that lets its guests live like the characters of an Austen novel. Jane has decided to use the vacation as the milestone. Once she has had her fun she will put Mr. Darcy behind herself, forever.<br /><br />Being myself, slightly obsessed with Jane Austen’s Pride and Prejudice, I couldn’t help but be sympathetic for Jane. And I love the idea of Pembrook Park. How much fun would that be! As far as the story I really enjoyed it! It is a bit of a romance, but that made me enjoy it all the more! This was the first novel by Shannon Hale that I have read, and I really value her writing style. I will be reading more from this author, and I must buy a copy of this book, I am sure I will be reading it again! <br /></span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/82561292?book_show_action=true">Dec 30, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kaethe Douglas" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kaethe Douglas" href="/user/show/1072582-kaethe-douglas">Kaethe Douglas</a>

        rated it

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1072582-kaethe-douglas?shelf=adventure">adventure</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1072582-kaethe-douglas?shelf=books-about-books">books-about-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1072582-kaethe-douglas?shelf=theater">theater</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1072582-kaethe-douglas?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1072582-kaethe-douglas?shelf=movies">movies</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1072582-kaethe-douglas?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer82561292" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15710337447595699552">If you are a fan of the works of Jane Austen, and particularly of the Jennifer Ehle/Colin Firth - starring mini-series of Pride and Prejudice, then an opportunity to spend three weeks vacation in a manor in England, live action role playing as an Austenesque heroine is a dream come true. Since this is an expensive proposition, (the home, the clothes, the food, the staff of actors, the horses even) our heroine Jane Hayes is lucky enough to receive such a trip from a great aunt who wishes to both </span>
  <span id="freeText15710337447595699552" style="display:none">If you are a fan of the works of Jane Austen, and particularly of the Jennifer Ehle/Colin Firth - starring mini-series of Pride and Prejudice, then an opportunity to spend three weeks vacation in a manor in England, live action role playing as an Austenesque heroine is a dream come true. Since this is an expensive proposition, (the home, the clothes, the food, the staff of actors, the horses even) our heroine Jane Hayes is lucky enough to receive such a trip from a great aunt who wishes to both indulge Jane and shake her out of her romantic fixation of Firth's Darcy.<br /><br />If, after the proceeding paragraph you're thinking "what a perfect Fantasy Island plot", you're going to love this as much as I did. Jane goes, she meets a couple of flirt-worthy men, she discovers how comfortable Regency clothes are and how uncomfortable 200-year-old manners can be.<br /><br />No doubt you've guessed that Jane learns important lessons and goes home a changed woman. But within the framework of a predictable plot, Hale has managed to work in a number of delightful surprises, even as she satisfies the reader's expectations.<br /><br />It is a charming work, and a more devoted homage to Austen than any "continuation" of Pride and Prejudice that I've ever attempted to read. I haven't enjoyed a work of Austenia so much since the movie Clueless.<br /><br />Library copy</span>
  <a data-text-id="15710337447595699552" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_11451734" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/11451734" />
    <a title="Danielle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/706164-danielle"><img alt="Danielle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1237176932p2/706164.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/11451734?book_show_action=true">Jan 02, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Danielle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Danielle" href="/user/show/706164-danielle">Danielle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">beach readers</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/706164-danielle?shelf=books-i-did-not-like">books-i-did-not-like</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer11451734" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14720892987638404107">Let's be realistic here: almost every female goes through their Jane Austen obsession phase. This book explores the "what if" of that obsession, and takes it to a whole new, somewhat unhealthy level.<br/><br/> Jane is your typical thirty-year-old woman that harbors a secret Darcy/Colin Firth obsession, which slowly begins to take over her life. In an attempt to help Jane discover herself, her deceased Aunt sets aside a vacation for Jane in her will- to Austenland. <br/><br/>When we first arrive at Austenland, the r</span>
  <span id="freeText14720892987638404107" style="display:none">Let's be realistic here: almost every female goes through their Jane Austen obsession phase. This book explores the "what if" of that obsession, and takes it to a whole new, somewhat unhealthy level.<br /><br /> Jane is your typical thirty-year-old woman that harbors a secret Darcy/Colin Firth obsession, which slowly begins to take over her life. In an attempt to help Jane discover herself, her deceased Aunt sets aside a vacation for Jane in her will- to Austenland. <br /><br />When we first arrive at Austenland, the reader is swept up along side Jane as she experiences the fantastical regency era in all its glory. Soon though, the book takes a hasty turn down junky romance lane. Along with love triangles and games, comedy relief characters, and a poorly fitted plot, Jane discovers that sometimes living with an obsession can be a dangerous thing, especially when you can't stop comparing fantasy to real life. <br /><br />If you enjoy reading light comedy romances, then Austenland is a suitable choice. If looking for a more substantial read, it would be better to search further. <br /><br />Out of Shannon Hale's other works [Goose Girl, Princess Academy, Etc.] this is a poor example of her writing and what she is capable of. I would strongly encourage anyone and everyone to read her other works, and enjoy!</span>
  <a data-text-id="14720892987638404107" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_149180260" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/149180260" />
    <a title="AMythicalBeast" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4823869-amythicalbeast"><img alt="AMythicalBeast" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1472965267p2/4823869.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/149180260?book_show_action=true">Feb 19, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="AMythicalBeast" class="user" itemprop="url" name="AMythicalBeast" href="/user/show/4823869-amythicalbeast">AMythicalBeast</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">no one in their right minds and definitely NOT to Austen fans</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to AMythicalBeast by: </span>
      Amazon
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4823869-amythicalbeast?shelf=reviewed-by-moi">reviewed-by-moi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4823869-amythicalbeast?shelf=awful-just-awful">awful-just-awful</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer149180260" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3037631233371487610">I had hopes for this- truly I did.<br/>By the cover and the cryptic jacket blurb I thought this was a paperback Lost in Austen. Hopefully better, because I couldn't stand that series and still can't believe BBC produced it. <br/>So. Girl is obsessed with Colin Firth in his Darcy persona. Old benefactor lady discovers this and (because she is rich and apparently totally understands such obsessions) buys her a three week treat in Austenland- an English 'pretend' resort (disguised as an old manor house) wher</span>
  <span id="freeText3037631233371487610" style="display:none">I had hopes for this- truly I did.<br />By the cover and the cryptic jacket blurb I thought this was a paperback Lost in Austen. Hopefully better, because I couldn't stand that series and still can't believe BBC produced it. <br />So. Girl is obsessed with Colin Firth in his Darcy persona. Old benefactor lady discovers this and (because she is rich and apparently totally understands such obsessions) buys her a three week treat in Austenland- an English 'pretend' resort (disguised as an old manor house) where everyone speaks and acts as if they were back in Regency Era. By everyone, I mean rich Americans who lo-oved P&amp;P and can afford the price of the place.<br />The girl feels lonely and dejected amongst all the actors\holiday makers\rich regulars - and because she is a wannabe-Elizabeth, she, of course, hates the resident Darcy (in all his moody, cold and in-spurts-emotional glory) from the instant she sees him. <br />Oh no, wait. In that first instant she drools, then gets on with the hating. <br />Her Wickham is a gardener who is her only connection to the real world (because he watches american football and is oppressed by the Austenland organiser lady and compulsively ignored by all the house mates).<br />So finally, after a lot of unimaginative angst, you may ask me: does the girl get a happy ending or does she fly off- independent and free of her Darcy obsession?<br />Well- I answer- she realises that her Wickham is really a plot point made up by the Organiser-dragon-lady, because not all the 'guests' there want to romance english gentlemen who are Darcy's facsimiles. <br />She also realises that Darcy is a regular english guy- divorced, an actor, and a hurt man who desperately wants to escape reality. <br />And, she finally realises that the guy in the seat beside her, on her flight back home, is her true love- the sad eyed, confused Darcy-pretender. <br /><br />Then she screams and jumps off the plane.<br /><br />Okay, not really. But that, I think would have been a better ending.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3037631233371487610" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
